## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / concentration-time ODE models)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a concentration A(t), which is the canonical form of kinetic rate laws in chemistry. With only t and A available, the most likely relationships are mechanistic or empirical rate expressions dA/dt = f(A,t) capturing reaction order, reversibility/equilibrium approach, time-varying rate constants, or transport/catalyst effects.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order decay/production: dA_dt = c0 (constant-rate feed or zero-order kinetics)
- First-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A (unimolecular decay if c0<0; growth if c0>0)
- Second-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular or autocombination under simplifying assumptions)
- General power-law (nth-order): dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order fitting)
- Mixed first+second order (parallel pathways): dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (two concurrent consumption/production channels)
- Shifted linear relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = c0 * (A - c1) (approach to steady state A=c1 when c0<0)
- Reversible/approach-to-capacity form: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (replenishment toward a maximum or approach to equilibrium from below)
- Autocatalytic with depletion (capacity-limited): dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating at low A, slowing near A=c1)
- Time-ramped pseudo-first-order: dA_dt = A * (c0 + c1 * t) (rate coefficient varies approximately linearly in time)
- Exponentially deactivating activity/catalyst: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (if c1<0, effective rate decreases with time)
- Induction/activation buildup: dA_dt = c0 * A * (1 - exp(c1 * t)) (slow start then approaches pseudo-first-order; typically c0<0, c1<0)
- Transport/aging-limited rate coefficient (power of time): dA_dt = c0 * A * (t + c1)**c2 (e.g., diffusion boundary layer growth; often c2<0)
- Hyperbolic time-dependent inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A / (t + c1) (rate slows roughly like 1/t due to deactivation or resource limitation)
- Periodic forcing (e.g., illumination/modulation): dA_dt = c0 * A * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (time-periodic rate constant)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Reaction order identification: linear in A suggests first-order; quadratic in A suggests second-order; A**c captures non-integer/empirical orders.
- Equilibrium/steady-state behavior: terms like (A - c) or (c - A) imply relaxation toward a fixed point concentration set by c.
- Autocatalysis vs depletion: factors A*(c - A) indicate acceleration at low A and saturation/slowdown near a limiting concentration.
- Time-varying environment/catalyst: coefficients depending on t (c0 + c1*t) represent ramps; exp(c*t) factors represent multiplicative activation/deactivation processes.
- Induction periods: multipliers (1 - exp(c*t)) create delayed onset of reaction rate before reaching an asymptotic regime.
- Transport limitations: negative powers of (t + c) (i.e., (t+c)**c2 with c2<0) mimic diffusion-layer thickening or aging effects that slow kinetics over time.
- External modulation: sinusoidal dependence on t is a signature of periodically driven kinetics (light chopping, oscillatory temperature/flow).
- Physical plausibility constraints: for a decaying reactant A, dA_dt should be non-positive when A>0; models often include factors that go to 0 as A→0 to preserve nonnegativity.

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (CRK17)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A*exp(-c1*_s*t) + c2*_f*A**c3
Candidate formulas: 80

GT is the fixed function
\[
F(t,A)=\underbrace{0.2084703204063362\,A^{1/3}}_{\text{time-independent}} \;+\;\underbrace{\big(-0.6750544468008356\big)\,A\,e^{-0.0783132263146032\,t}}_{\text{linear in }A,\ \text{single exponential in }t}.
\]
So any matching candidate must be able to represent **exactly** “(constant)\(A^{1/3}\) + (constant)\(A e^{kt}\)” with **no other nonzero dependence** on \(t\) or \(A\). Also note GT uses \(A\), not \(|A|\); unless the domain is restricted to \(A\ge 0\), any \(|A|\) term cannot equal \(A\) for all real \(A\).

Below, for each candidate, I check whether we can choose its free constants to reduce it to exactly the GT form.

---

### 1. `A**(1/3)*c0 + A**c1*c2/(A**c1 + c3) + c4*exp(c5*t)*Abs(A)`
Has a rational-in-\(A\) term \(A^{c1}c2/(A^{c1}+c3)\) which cannot be identically 0 for all \(A\) unless \(c2=0\). Then remaining has \(|A|e^{c5 t}\), not \(A e^{kt}\) for all real \(A\). **No match**.

### 2. `A**(1/3)*c0 + c1*exp(c2*t)*Abs(A)`
Same issue: \(|A|\) vs \(A\). Cannot equal GT for all real \(A\). **No match**.

### 3. `A**(1/3)*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t)`
This is exactly the GT structure. Choose:
- \(c0 = 0.2084703204063362\)
- \(c1 = -0.6750544468008356\)
- \(c2 = -0.0783132263146032\)

Then candidate 3 equals GT for all \(t,A\). **Match**.

### 4. `A**(1/3)*c0 + c1*exp(c2*t)*Abs(A) + c3*exp(c4*sin(c5*t + c6))`
Can set \(c3=0\) to drop the last term, but still has \(|A|\). **No match**.

### 5. `A**(1/3)*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*sin(...)`
Set \(c3=0\). Remaining matches GT form; pick \(c0,c1,c2\) as in (3). **Match**.

### 6. `A**(1/3)*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*(...)^(...)`
Set \(c3=0\). Remaining matches GT with same parameter choice. **Match**.

### 7. `A**(1/3)*c0 + A*c1/(c2*t + c3) + c4*exp(c5*t)*Abs(A) + c6/(c2*t + c3)`
To remove rational-in-\(t\) terms need \(c1=0\) and \(c6=0\). Then left with \(|A|e^{c5 t}\) again. **No match**.

### 8. `A**(1/3)*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + A*c3/(c4*t + c5) + c6/(c4*t + c5)`
Need \(c3=0,c6=0\) to remove rational terms. Then reduces to candidate (3) form. **Match**.

### 9. `A**c0*c1 + c2*exp(c3*t) + c4*log(A*c5 + 1) + c6*(c7 + Abs(A))**c8*exp(c9*t)`
Contains log and \((c7+|A|)^{c8}\) unless coefficients set to 0; can set \(c4=0,c6=0\). Then left with \(c1 A^{c0} + c2 e^{c3 t}\), which cannot produce \(A e^{kt}\) (product of \(A\) and exponential). **No match**.

### 10. `A**(1/3)*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*exp(c4*t)*Abs(A)`
To avoid extra \(|A|e^{c4 t}\) term, set \(c3=0\). Then matches (3). **Match**.

### 11. `A**(1/3)*c0 + A**2*c1*exp(c2*t) + A*c3*exp(c4*t)`
Need to eliminate \(A^2 e^{...}\): set \(c1=0\). Then have \(A c3 e^{c4 t}\) plus \(A^{1/3}\) term: matches GT by choosing \(c3=-0.6750544...\), \(c4=-0.0783132...\), \(c0=0.2084703...\). **Match**.

### 12. `A**(1/3)*c0 + A**c1*c2*log(c3*t + 1) + c4*exp(c5*t)*Abs(A)`
Log-in-\(t\) term must vanish: set \(c2=0\). Still \(|A|\) term remains. **No match**.

### 13. `A**(1/3)*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + A*c3*exp(c4*t)*sin(c5*t + c6)`
Set \(c3=0\). Then matches (3). **Match**.

### 14. `A**(1/3)*c0 + c1*exp(c2*t)*Abs(A) + c3*exp(A*c4)`
Set \(c3=0\) removes \(e^{A c4}\), but \(|A|\) remains. **No match**.

### 15. `A**(1/3)*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*exp(A*c4)`
Set \(c3=0\). Then matches (3). **Match**.

### 16. `A**(1/3)*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*Abs(A)**c4/(c5 + Abs(A)**c4)`
Set \(c3=0\). Then matches (3). **Match**.

### 17. `A**(1/3)*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3`
GT has no constant offset, so set \(c3=0\). Then matches (3). **Match**.

### 18. `A**(1/3)*c0 + c1*exp(c2*t)*Abs(A) + c3`
Even with \(c3=0\), has \(|A|\). **No match**.

### 19. `A**(1/3)*c0 + c1*exp(c2*t)*Abs(A) + c3*log(c4*exp(A**c5*c6) + 1)`
Set \(c3=0\) removes log term, still \(|A|\). **No match**.

### 20. `A**(1/3)*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + A**c3*c4`
Need no extra \(A^{c3}\) term: set \(c4=0\). Then matches (3). **Match**.

### 21. `A**(1/3)*c0 + A**c1*c2 + c3*exp(c4*t)*Abs(A)`
To get \(A e^{kt}\) we’d need the exponential term to be \(A e^{kt}\) but it’s \(|A|e^{...}\). Also the \(A^{c1}\) term must vanish (set \(c2=0\)). Still \(|A|\). **No match**.

### 22. `A**(1/3)*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*log(A*c4 + 1)`
Set \(c3=0\). Then matches (3). **Match**.

### 23. `A**(1/3)*c0 + c1*exp(c2*t)*Abs(A) + c3*log(A*c4 + 1)`
Even with \(c3=0\), has \(|A|\). **No match**.

### 24. `A**(1/3)*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*Abs(A)`
Set \(c3=0\). Then matches (3). **Match**.

### 25. `A**(1/3)*c0 + A*c1/(A + c2) + c3*exp(c4*t)*Abs(A)`

**Candidate 10:** `A^(1/3)*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*exp(c4*t)*|A|`. With A≥0: `c0*A^(1/3) + (c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*exp(c4*t))*A`. Set c3=0. **MATCH**

**Candidate 11:** `A^(1/3)*c0 + A^2*c1*exp(c2*t) + A*c3*exp(c4*t)`. Set c1=0. **MATCH**
